                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">شَعِيرٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Msb, K,) which may be also pronounced <foreign lang="ar">شِعِيرٌ</foreign>, agreeably with the dial. of Temeem, as may any word of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِيلٌ</foreign> of which the medial radical letter is a faucial, and, accord. to Lth, certain of the Arabs pronounced in a similar manner any word of that measure of which the medial radical letter is not a faucial, like <foreign lang="ar">كَبِيرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">جَلِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَرِيمٌ</foreign>, (MF,) [and thus do many in the present day, others pronouncing the fet-h in this case, more correctly, in the manner termed <foreign lang="ar">إِمَالَة</foreign>, i. e. as “ e ” in our word “ bed: ” <hi rend="ital">Barley;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a certain grain,</hi> (S, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">well known:</hi> (Msb, K:) of the masc. gender, except in the dial. of the people of Nejd, who make it fem.: (Zj, Msb:) n. un. with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> [signifying <hi rend="ital">a barleycorn</hi>]. (S, K.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">An accompanying associate;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">عَشِيرٌ مُصَاحِبٌ</foreign>: on the authority of En-Nawawee: (K, TA:) said to be formed by transposition: but it may be from <foreign lang="ar">شَعَرَهَا</foreign> meaning “ he slept with her in one <foreign lang="ar">شِعَار</foreign>; ” [see 3; and so originally signifying <hi rend="ital">a person who sleeps with another in one innermost garment;</hi>] then applied to any special companion.                   <hi rend="ital">A poet:</hi> (T, S, Msb, K:) so called because of his intelligence; (S, Msb;) or because he knows what others know not: (T, TA:) accord. to Akh, it is a possessive epithet, like <foreign lang="ar">لَابِنٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">تَامِرٌ</foreign>: (S:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">شُعَرَآءُ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) deviating from analogy: (S, Msb:) Sb says that the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَاعِلٌ</foreign> is likened in this case to <foreign lang="ar">فَعِيلٌ</foreign>; and hence this pl.: (TA:) or, accord. to IKh, the pl. is of this form because the sing. is from <foreign lang="ar">شَعُرَ</foreign>, and therefore should by rule be of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِيلٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">شَرِيفٌ</foreign> [from <foreign lang="ar">شَرُفَ</foreign>]; but were it so, it might be confounded with <foreign lang="ar">شَعِير</foreign> meaning the grain thus called, therefore they said <foreign lang="ar">شَاعِرٌ</foreign>, and regarded in the pl. the original form of the sing. (Msb.) A wonderful poet is called <foreign lang="ar">خِنْذِيذٌ</foreign>: one next below him, <foreign lang="ar">شَاعِرٌ</foreign>: then,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22491-1" target="شَوَيْعِرٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [the dim.]: (Yoo, K:) then,
